<review>Although we didn't eat at this place, this place is noticable from driving by and small. Today was a rainy day so great day to eat pizza or hot foods. No parking unless you park on the green curb on the side. I ordered 2 Medium Calzones for me and my sister, I think it's an okay price for a Medium, especially when I first saw it, thinking it's a XL. The only small thing is that when I first took a bite of mine, it felt kind of salty but after that, it was fine. My sister said that it has too much sauce, her Calzone broke when pushing it in. Where as I noticed that it was pretty much empty if you got it all puffy, expecting it to be filled with cheese and pepperoni like a hot Pocket. To enjoy it, you'd have to smash it like a tortilla, not literally, but basically like a quesadilla. <rating>4< /rating>< Review>
THE BEST PIZZA! Hands down...and there are a LOT of hands. I was very skeptical when my sister (Hana J.) mentioned we try. But pizza sounded good on a cold rainy night, so we went for it. She called ahead (thank goodness), cuz if we didn't, we'd have to wait a long long time. By the time we got to the place, our pizza was in the works, and I think we only waited about 20 min max. The guy makes all the pizzas by hand, by himself, in this crazy small shop. He's super friendly and sweet. He tries to remember people's names too, for future visits!Maximo's Pizza< /Review>

<Rate>1</Rate><text>I visited Diamond's on Thursday, March 10, 2016 around 7pm. There's no seating ... take out only (but there is plenty of room for at least 4 tables / 16 seats).

The combo burger meal seemed reasonably priced, so I order it  (cheeseburger, med fries, med drink ... $4.99). I saw they also have Parmesan Garlic fries for $1.99 ($0.50 more the reg fries), so I asked for a substitution & I would pay the difference. The cashier wanted to bill me $1.99 extra, no just $0.50. I questioned him about it, he took it to his boss and the boss said to charge me $0.75 extra. OK, I can live with that.

So I pay and he gives me my drink and I wait 10+ minutes for the food, by which time I'm over halfway done with the drink. So when I get the food, I asked for a "top off" (refill), to which I'm told they charge for refills. Wow, their only competition in a 5+ mile radius is a Mexican restaurant and a bar ... and this is the way they do business? Every other burger joint that I've been to in Barstow gives free refills as long as you haven't left the premises.

Oh, and they gave my order to me in a Togo's bag!

The burger was ok, the fries were good and the drink was ... a drink. And I'll never go there again.

< UserId.>
107959890263716597774< /UserId.>
<username>Tommy Mack< /username>< Date>
1606759259833< /Date>
< Rate>
1</Rate>
< text>
This is probably one of the worst place to receive your motorcycle training and certification if you're a complete beginner. Honda Rider markets one of its Basic Riding Course for novices but has failed to provide proper trainings and oversights of vehicle controls as they'll immediately settle for Pass/Fail to beginners who were not often briefed properly. Much of the time, these lessons were given verbally in an open environment and proportionately away from students who would not be able to comprehend the instructor's information.

Furthermore, despite being a Basic Riding Course, the program allows anyone with higher level riding experience to attend the course, thus downplaying the struggles that beginners would have to face when learning how to ride a motorcycle for the very first time. While experienced riders will be able to waive the DMV riding portion upon successful completion, this privilege however ruins the experience for other new riders as their performance are often graded amongst their peers, as a result, the classroom environment is often rushed and beginners face a no-refund elimination if they're not able to comprehend new lesson for the very first time.

Overall, I cannot recommend Honda Rider Education Center as a place for new riders to visit, due to complete disregards in empathy for new riders, improperly rushed operational guideline of motorized vehicle, and a no refund for an expensive Basic Riding Course. From my perspective as one of the students in Q1 2020, the instructors were focusing more on finding students to fail as oppose to helping students navigate their ways  through remediation. While the common excuses seem to be aimed at the fact that there wouldn't have been enough time as these instructors were going by CMSP guideline or students were removed as they might have posed risks for other riders, this appears more as cop-out excuses when considering that students were immediately placed on the challenging course before they were even trained for the CMSP qualification, there were also hardly any hand on training or familiarization with the vehicle before mounting the motorcycle, and that students were dismissed without knowing there were even second attempts, which can only be scheduled by phone call, as opposed to on site.

For recommendation on how to handle a motorcycle, new riders are better off hiring a one on one tutoring session with someone else and passing the DMV riding portion using a scooter, as the fees would be equivalent to attending the Basic Riding Course but the learning outcomes and success would be higher. I would also highly recommend watching YouTube videos on motorcycle fundamentals from channels such as "BLOCKHEAD" or "DanDanTheFireman" as they'll go over clear important instructions of motorcycle controls, something that the Honda Riding program won't cover and many novices will fail as a direct result.

On the positive side, one of the instructor appears professional and informative both in classroom and outdoor. However, due to the learning structure of this Basic Riding Course, I still cannot recommend any beginners attend this program due to high risk of failing and poor learning outcomes, especially for a non-refundable price tag.

Pros:
Clean facility
Some of the instructors were friendly
Provided helmets and motorcycles

Cons:
- No refund
- Extremely fast pace for beginner riders
- More experienced students than first timers
- Improper and unclear instructions
- Easy to be removed for your first mistake
- Not enough suitable bikes for beginners
- Lack of one on one guidance
- Not enough repetition for mental exercise
- Revisit can only be scheduled through phone< /text>

<Review>As far as I'm concerned, this is THE BEST & ONLY PLACE to go to! I previously took the CMSP class with another joker company, & I wish to God I had known about Honda first. Quite honestly though, who but someone like Honda, really KNOWS how to teach people how to ride?!  I won't go anywhere else, ever again. You really shouldn't have to learn how to ride in the back of someone's parking lot on shoddy equipment from people that just "know" how to ride.

HONDA DOES IT RIGHT -- from start to finish.

The Honda instructors were some of the best instructors I've ever had, hands down. The curriculum was tight. The equipment & facilities were above & beyond top notch. Even their LOANER gear was high-end (helmets, boots, gloves, jerseys). I never once felt like I was in an unsafe environment (unlike that "other" company...). Our instructors were as awesome as it can get -- encouraging, engaging, positive, thorough, etc. There was never a single moment where you were left wondering how you were doing, or where you could improve. They actually ENCOURAGED questions & feedback! Go figure!

They don't overbook their classes & keep it at a very manageable 12-person max. My class was amazing & fun! Everyone encouraged each other, & it made the experience that much better.

The track is fully lit up & definitely helps not cooking out there with the sun blazing in your eyes (but don't worry, the facilities have misters!).

Without riding a bike since 2009 (almost 5 years), because the cost was reasonnable ($250) and I felt like I would have a better chance to succeed than at the DMV, I went with them. Coaches have memorized the lines that are required to announce and give a sarcastic tone of voice. During practice the coaches fail to pay 100% close attention to the individual during the course. During the test the coaches assume you know the instructions and do not repeat. Management is very rude and backs up what the coaches tell them rather than dealing with matters professionally. COURSE DOES NOT TEACH REAL LIFE ISSUES AND PRACTICE DOES NOT GIVE ACCURATE REAL LIFE EVENTS AS THEY SHOULD! For example, course does not exceed 20mph, does not give accurate turning posture (coaches require you to look "into the turn" which voids the riders blindspot in real life. Coaches do not pull each individual aside rather the coaches give a short verbal suggestion in which is assumed the student knows what is suggested. Coaches DO NOT give a accurate slow paced example of what is required, rather they speed through the instructions and example but quickly and rarely ask "You guys ready? Gear up and let's go!" While 4/6 student riders ponder on what is required on every course. Last but not least, the in-classroom teaching is a very basic and bland dvd that is put on while the instructor leaves the room. The written test is a JOKE! The instructor leaves the room while everyone cheats by looking in the books and/or the students cheat off each other. Regardless of the individual students prior knowledge, each student is assumed to be up to par after the small practice is done, if not the coaches say,"Looks like you need some practice, you can either retake the class when your ready or you can sit back and watch". Which basically is the coaches way of not doing their job and instructing the student and kicking them out of class; they're idea behind it is stating you are a "safety risk" but in reality 2/3 of the students never sat on a bike and/or don't have a bike to practice on so retaking the class would be a chance for another failure when the coach SHOULD coach the student on what should be corrected.
Also, prices are ridiculous in the idea that YouTube teaches ALOT more real life scenarios rather than having a person tell you if your a good motorcyclist or not. I personally have put in over 15,000+ miles on my personal motorcycle but multiple students who are obviously fearful and make unsteady turns at less than 20mph are considered better drivers than me. I honestly say this place is a joke but the idea of getting reduced insurance and the viod of the dmv test is the only reason why I took the course. If you are taking it to learn, go on YouTube and avoid spending the $150-$250 hefty price tag and learn yourself! You'll learn more being on YOUR own bike since YOUR going to be riding that and not the bike they have you use.
NOTHING is taught about street lights, stop lights, blindspots, badly paved streets and weather, nor anything to do with real-life emergencies.<//Text>
